The Reductio Against Assuming Independence
Razi reduces all possibilities of the servant being able to choose the opposite to absurdity or determinism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi's argument shows that even if the servant can choose the opposite, every possible explanation leads to an absurdity or determinism.

Core Idea
Allowing the servant to choose the opposite forces logical contradictions or determinism.

Having established the simple case, Razi now tackles the more challenging alternative: suppose the servant can indeed choose the opposite. This opens a complex reductio argument. Through an exhaustive analysis of the sources and necessity of a determining factor (murajjih), Razi shows that every conceivable path leads either to an infinite regress, to coercion (jabr), or to a denial of causal principles—all of which undermine the claim of human independence. This lesson walks you through this intricate logical tree.

Guided Path
1
Read the full alternative branch
Read the Arabic passage from 'وأما إن صح منه الترك' to the end of the provided text. Try to follow the logical flow of possibilities.
2
Identify the three sources of the murajjih
Notice that Razi divides the determining factor into three possible origins: from the servant, from God, or from neither. List them.
3
Trace the consequences of each source
For each source, follow the sub‑arguments. The first leads to infinite regress, the second to either necessity (jabr) or regress, the third to events without an originator.
Pay special attention to the intricate sub‑case under 'from God' where the preference does not reach necessity.
4
Consider the case without murajjih
Razi also considers the possibility that the preference does not require any determining factor at all. See how this leads to coincidence and ultimately to jabr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى : أن العبد حال ما رجح الفعل هل يصح منه ترجيح الترك بدلا عن الفعل، أو لا يصح ؟ فإن كان حال كونه مصدرا للفعل، لا يصح منه الترك. وحال كونه مصدرا للترك، لا يصح منه الفعل، فحينئذ العبد غير مستقل لا بالفعل ولا بالترك وذلك هو المطلوب وأما إن صح منه الترك بدلا عن الفعل، فترجيح أحد الطرفين على الآخر، إما أن يتوقف على مرجح أو لا يتوقف . فإن توقف على مرجح ، فذلك المرجح إما أن يكون من العبد أو من الله تعالى، أو لا من العبد ولا الله . فإن كان من العبد عاد التقسيم الأول. ويلزم التسلسل، وإن كان من تعالى . فنقول : عند حصول ذلك المرجح ، قد صار الفعل راجحًا على الترك. ونقول : ذلك الرجحان إما أن يقال: إنه انتهى إلى حد الوجوب، أو ما انتهى إلى حد الوجوب . فإن كان الأول هو الحق، لزم الجبر، لأنه على تقدير حصول ذلك المرجح، صار الفعل واجب الوقوع، وعلى تقدير أن لا يحصل، كان الفعل ممتنع الوقوع . وإن كان الثاني، هو الحق، وهو أنه ما انتهي إلى حد الوجوب . فنقول : إذا كان الأمر كذلك كان عند حصول ذلك المرجح لا يمتنع حصول ذلك الفعل تارة وعدم حصوله أخرى. وكل ما كان ممكنا لا يلزم من فرض وقوعه محال. فلنفرضه تارة ،واقعا وأخرى غير واقع فاختصاص أحد الوقتين بالوقوع، والثاني بعدم الوقوع . إما أن يتوقف على انضمام قيد زائد إليه أو لا يتوقف فإن توقف لم يكن الذي حصل أولا، تمام المرجح لأنه كان لا بد معه من هذا القيد . لكنا كنا فرضنا ما حصل أولا، تمام المرجح، هذا خلف. وأيضا : فإنه يعود التقسيم في المجموع الحاصل من المرجح الأول، ومن هذا القيد . فإن لم يصر الرجحان واجبا افتقر إلى مرجح آخر، ولزم التسلسل. وهو محال . وإن وجب، عاد ما ذكرناه من لزوم الجبر وأما إن كان اختصاص أحد الوقتين بالوقوع، لا يتوقف على انضمام قيد زائد إلى ما كان حاصلا أولا، مع أن نسبة ذلك المرجح الذي كان حاصلا أولا إلى وقتي الوقوع واللاوقوع على السوية، لزم رجحان أحد طرفي الممكن المتساوي على الآخر من غير مرجح. وهو محال. وأما القسم الثالث : وهو أن يحدث ذلك المرجح لا من العبد ولا من الله تعالى. فهذا يقتضي حدوث الحادثات لا عن محدث. وتجويزه يبطل القول بالاستدلال بحدوث الحوادث على وجود الله تعالى . وهذا باطل. هذا كله إذا قلنا بأن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل يصح منه الترك بدلا عن الفعل، إلا أن هذا الرجحان يتوقف على مرجح أما إذا قلنا: إنه لا يتوقف على المرجح، فحينئذ قد حصل الرجحان لا عن مؤثر. وتجويزه يبطل القول بافتقار الجائزات إلى المؤثر والمرجح، ويلزم منه نفي الصانع. وأيضا فبتقدير أن يكون الأمر كذلك، وجب أن يكون ذلك الرجحان واقعا بالاتفاق بمعنى أنه يكون واقعا لا لأمر صدر عن الفعل. وهذا أيضا يقتضي الجبر، لأنه إذا وقع ذلك الاتفاق، حصل الفعل سواء أراد أو لم يرد . وإذا لم يقع لم يحصل الفعل، سواء أراد أو لم يرد. فيكون الجبر لازما أيضا على هذا التقدير. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : ثبت أن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل. إن صح الترك فإما أن يتوقف ذلك الترجيح على المرجح أو لا يتوقف، وثبت أن القسمين
The first proof: that when the servant prefers the action, is it valid for him to prefer the opposite instead of the action, or not? If, when he is the source of the action, it is not valid for him to prefer the opposite, and when he is the source of refraining, it is not valid for him to perform the action, then the servant is not independent either in action or in refraining, and that is what is desired. But if it is valid for him to prefer the opposite instead of the action, then the preference of one of the two sides over the other either depends on a determining factor (murajjih) or does not depend. If it depends on a determining factor, then that determining factor is either from the servant, or from God Almighty, or neither from the servant nor from God. If it is from the servant, the first division returns and an infinite regress (tasalsul) follows. If it is from God Almighty, we say: when that determining factor occurs, the action has become preferred over refraining. And we say: that preference either, it is said, reaches the limit of necessity (wujub) or does not reach the limit of necessity. If the first is true, jabr (determinism) is necessary, because on the assumption that the determining factor occurs, the action becomes necessary of occurrence, and on the assumption that it does not occur, the action becomes impossible of occurrence. And if the second is true, namely that it does not reach the limit of necessity, we say: if the matter is such, then when that determining factor occurs it is not impossible that the action occurs sometimes and does not occur at other times. And everything that is possible, its supposition as occurring does not necessitate impossibility. So let us suppose it sometimes occurring and other times not occurring. Then the specification of one of the two times with occurrence and the other with non-occurrence either depends on the addition of an extra condition to it or does not depend. If it depends, then that which occurred first was not the complete determining factor, because there must be this condition along with it. But we had assumed that what occurred first is the complete determining factor; this is a contradiction (khalaf). Also, the division returns concerning the total obtained from the first determining factor and this condition. If the preference does not become necessary, it needs another determining factor, and infinite regress follows, which is impossible. And if it becomes necessary, then what we mentioned of the necessity of jabr returns. As for if the specification of one of the two times with occurrence does not depend on the addition of an extra condition to what was present first, while the relation of that determining factor which was present first to the two times of occurrence and non-occurrence is equal, then a preference of one side of the possible equal over the other without a determining factor is necessary, which is impossible. As for the third division: that the determining factor occurs neither from the servant nor from God Almighty; this necessitates the occurrence of events without an originator (muhdith). And allowing it invalidates the argument from the occurrence of events for the existence of God Almighty, and this is false. All this if we say that when the servant is the source of the action, it is valid for him to prefer the opposite instead of the action, but that this preference depends on a determining factor. But if we say that it does not depend on a determining factor, then the preference occurs without any influence (mu'aththir). And allowing it invalidates the statement that contingent things need an effective cause and a determining factor, and it necessitates the denial of the Creator. Also, on the assumption that the matter is such, that preference must occur by coincidence (ittifaq), meaning that it occurs not for a reason derived from the action. This also necessitates jabr, because if that coincidence occurs, the action occurs whether he wills or not, and if it does not occur, the action does not occur whether he wills or not. Thus jabr is also necessary on this assumption. If you understand this, we say: it is established that when the servant is the source of the action, if refraining is valid, then that preference either depends on a determining factor or does not depend, and it is established that the two divisions...
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This is a complex proof by contradiction. The passage begins with the first argument: consider the servant at the moment of preferring the action. Is it possible for him to prefer the opposite instead? If not, then when he does the action, he cannot choose otherwise, and when he refrains, he cannot act, so he is not independent—this is the desired conclusion. If he can prefer the opposite, then this preference needs a determining factor (murajjih). That determining factor must come either from the servant, from God, or from neither. If from the servant, then the same question recurs, leading to infinite regress. If from God, then once that factor is present, the action becomes preferred. Does this preference reach necessity? If yes, then determinism (jabr) follows because given the factor the action must occur, and without it it is impossible. If it does not reach necessity, then the action remains possible, but then we can suppose it occurs at one time and not at another; the allocation of one time over the other either requires an additional condition or not. If it requires a condition, then the initial factor was not fully decisive, contradicting the assumption, and the same division recurs, leading to regress or necessity. If no additional condition is needed, then the original factor has equal relation to both times, so the preference of one time over the other would be without a determining factor, which is impossible. The third case, that the determining factor comes from neither servant nor God, implies events without an originator, which destroys the argument from contingency for God's existence. Finally, if we suppose that no determining factor is needed at all, then the preference occurs without any influence, which also negates the need for an effective cause and implies denial of the Creator, and also implies jabr because the action occurs by chance regardless of will. Thus all possibilities lead to either jabr or absurdity, proving that the servant is not independent.

رجحان بلا مرجح
اختصاص الوقتين
الممكن
المؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Razi's proof assumes determinism from the start, but it is a reductio that shows all alternatives lead to absurdity or determinism.
Correction: The proof does not assume determinism; it examines the assumption that the servant can choose the opposite and shows that it inevitably leads to determinism or logical impossibility.

Checkpoint
In the case where no determining factor is needed for the preference, what does Razi conclude?
A) The servant is free.
B) It leads to jabr (determinism).
C) It leads to infinite regress.
D) It proves the existence of God.

Key Takeaway
Even if the servant can choose the opposite, every possible explanation leads to a logical contradiction or determinism, proving that true independence is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a choice, do you truly believe your decision is independent of Allah's power? How does Razi's reductio challenge your sense of autonomy, and what does that mean for your daily reliance on Him?
?
If every possibility of human independence leads to absurdity or jabr, what does that imply for your responsibility for your actions? Can you still feel accountable while accepting that Allah is the ultimate creator of your choices? How should that change how you approach sin and repentance?
?
Razi shows that assuming we can choose the opposite forces a logical dead end. Have you ever acted as if your choices are entirely your own, without recognizing that every outcome depends on Allah? What would it look like for you to live with the conviction that all your actions are determined by His will, yet you are still commanded to obey?

Divine Decree

The Dilemma of Preponderance: Necessity, Regress, or Absurdity
Razi enumerates and refutes possible ways a preponderant factor could determine an act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's initial argument that any preponderant factor for a possible act leads either to the act's necessity, an infinite regress, or an absurd preponderance without cause.

Core Idea
A possible act's occurrence requires a preponderant factor, which inevitably leads to determinism or absurdity.

Razi begins by stating the problem: if a preponderant factor determines an act, does the act become necessary? He then explores the case where the act remains possible but requires a preponderant factor. The analysis reveals that any attempt to explain the specification of occurrence without leading to contradiction fails, ultimately supporting determinism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main alternatives
Read the Arabic carefully. Notice that Razi first presents two possibilities: either the act becomes necessary upon the preponderant factor, or it does not. He then focuses on the second case.
This sets up the entire argument.
2
Trace the argument about specification
Razi argues that if the act is possible and occurs at one time but not another, the specification must either depend on an extra condition or not. Work through each branch.
The branch of dependence leads to infinite regress or necessity; the branch of independence leads to preponderance without cause.
3
Understand the third division
The third possibility—that the preponderant factor comes from neither servant nor God—is dismissed as it would imply events without an originator, undermining the proof for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية والعشرون
المرجح، صار الفعل واجب الوقوع، وعلى تقدير أن لا يحصل، كان الفعل ممتنع الوقوع . وإن كان الثاني، هو الحق، وهو أنه ما انتهي إلى حد الوجوب . فنقول : إذا كان الأمر كذلك كان عند حصول ذلك المرجح لا يمتنع حصول ذلك الفعل تارة وعدم حصوله أخرى. وكل ما كان ممكنا لا يلزم من فرض وقوعه محال.
فلنفرضه تارة واقعا وأخرى غير واقع فاختصاص أحد الوقتين بالوقوع، والثاني بعدم الوقوع . إما أن يتوقف على انضمام قيد زائد إليه أو لا يتوقف فإن توقف لم يكن الذي حصل أولا تمام المرجح لأنه كان لا بد معه من هذا القيد . لكنا كنا فرضنا ما حصل أولا تمام المرجح، هذا خلف.
وأيضا : فإنه يعود التقسيم في المجموع الحاصل من المرجح الأول، ومن هذا القيد . فإن لم يصر الرجحان واجبا افتقر إلى مرجح آخر، ولزم التسلسل. وهو محال . وإن وجب، عاد ما ذكرناه من لزوم الجبر وأما إن كان اختصاص أحد الوقتين بالوقوع، لا يتوقف على انضمام قيد زائد إلى ما كان حاصلا أولا، مع أن نسبة ذلك المرجح الذي كان حاصلا أولا إلى وقتي الوقوع واللاوقوع على السوية، لزم رجحان أحد طرفي الممكن المتساوي على الآخر من غير مرجح. وهو محال. وأما القسم الثالث : وهو أن يحدث ذلك المرجح لا من العبد ولا من الله تعالى. فهذا يقتضي حدوث الحادثات لا عن محدث. وتجويزه يبطل القول بالاستدلال بحدوث الحوادث على وجود الله تعالى . وهذا باطل.
هذا كله إذا قلنا بأن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل يصح منه الترك بدلا عن الفعل، إلا أن هذا الرجحان يتوقف على مرجح أما إذا قلنا: إنه لا يتوقف على المرجح، فحينئذ قد حصل الرجحان لا عن مؤثر. وتجويزه يبطل القول بافتقار الجائزات إلى المؤثر والمرجح، ويلزم منه نفي الصانع. وأيضا فبتقدير أن يكون الأمر كذلك، وجب أن يكون ذلك الرجحان واقعا بالاتفاق بمعنى أنه يكون واقعا لا لأمر صدر عن الفعل. وهذا أيضا يقتضي الجبر، لأنه إذا وقع ذلك الاتفاق، حصل الفعل سواء أراد أو لم يرد . وإذا لم يقع لم يحصل الفعل، سواء أراد أو لم يرد. فيكون الجبر لازما أيضا على هذا التقدير.
إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : ثبت أن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل. إن صح الترك فإما أن يتوقف ذلك الترجيح على المرجح أو لا يتوقف، وثبت أن القسمين باطلان، فثبت أن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل يمتنع منه الترك. وحال كونه مصدرا للترك، يمتنع منه الفعل.
The twenty-second issue. If the preponderant factor exists, the act becomes necessary of occurrence, and on the assumption that it does not occur, the act becomes impossible of occurrence. If the second is the truth, that it did not reach the limit of necessity. We say: If such is the case, then when that preponderant factor is present, it is not impossible for that act to occur sometimes and not occur at other times. And everything that is possible, it is not necessary from assuming its occurrence an absurdity. So let us assume it sometimes occurring and sometimes not occurring. The specification of one of the two times by occurrence and the second by non-occurrence either depends on the addition of an extra condition or does not depend. If it depends, then what first occurred was not the complete preponderant factor, because this condition was necessarily with it. But we had assumed what first occurred to be the complete preponderant factor—that is a contradiction. Also, the division returns to the aggregate consisting of the first preponderant factor and this condition. If the preponderance does not become necessary, it requires another preponderant factor, leading to infinite regress—which is impossible. And if it becomes necessary, then what we mentioned of the necessity of determinism returns. But if the specification of one of the two times by occurrence does not depend on the addition of an extra condition to what was first present, while the relation of that preponderant factor which was first present to the two times of occurrence and non-occurrence is equal, then the preponderance of one side of the possible over the other without a preponderant factor follows—which is impossible. As for the third division: that the preponderant factor occurs neither from the servant nor from God Almighty; this entails the occurrence of events without an originator, and allowing it invalidates the argument from the occurrence of events for the existence of God Almighty—and this is false. All this if we say that the servant, while being the source of the act, it is possible for him to refrain instead of the act, except that this preponderance depends on a preponderant factor. But if we say that it does not depend on a preponderant factor, then preponderance has occurred without an effective agent, and allowing it invalidates the statement that contingent things need an effective agent and a preponderant factor, and it entails the denial of the Maker. Also, assuming that such is the case, that preponderance must be occurring by chance, meaning it occurs without something issuing from the act. This also entails determinism, because if that chance occurs, the act occurs whether he wills or does not will; if it does not occur, the act does not occur whether he wills or does not will. Thus determinism is necessary on this assumption as well. If you have understood this, we say: It is established that the servant, while being the source of the act, if refraining is possible, then that preponderance either depends on a preponderant factor or does not, and it is established that both divisions are false. Thus it is established that the servant, while being the source of the act, cannot refrain; and while being the source of refraining, cannot act.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument about preponderance (tarjih) and its implications for human free will. Razi begins by considering two possibilities regarding the preponderant factor that determines an act: either the act becomes necessary when the factor is present, or not. He then examines the scenario where the act is possible but requires a preponderant factor. He argues that if the specification of one time over another for occurrence depends on an additional condition, then the initial factor was not truly complete, leading to infinite regress or determinism. If no additional condition is needed but the factor relates equally to both times, then preponderance occurs without cause, which is absurd. A third division—that the preponderant factor comes from neither servant nor God—invalidates the argument for God's existence. Razi then shifts to the condition where the servant can possibly refrain. He shows that if the preponderance depends on a factor, determinism follows via regress; if not, preponderance occurs by chance, again determinism. The conclusion is that when the servant is the source of the act, refraining is impossible; when the source of refraining, acting is impossible. This is a key argument for determinism (jabr) in Ash'ari thought, aiming to show that human acts are ultimately necessitated.

Key Terms
المرجح
الوجوب
الامتناع
التسلسل
الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a preponderant factor can simply make an act possible without further consequences.
Correction: Razi shows that any account of how the act occurs at one time rather than another leads to either necessity, regress, or an uncaused preponderance—all problematic.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's argument, what happens if the specification of occurrence depends on an extra condition?
A) The act becomes freely chosen.
B) The initial preponderant factor was complete.
C) Either an infinite regress or determinism follows.
D) The act becomes impossible.

Key Takeaway
Any preponderant factor for a possible act either leads to determinism, infinite regress, or an absurd preponderance without cause—eliminating alternatives to determinism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi argues that the only coherent conclusion is that your every action is necessitated by a preponderant factor. Does this truth make you more responsible or less? Examine your heart: do you sometimes hide behind the divine decree to avoid accountability? What would change in your life today if you truly believed that every choice you make is determined by God's will and your own character?
?
If the preponderant factor leads to determinism, then your next breath, your next thought, your next act of worship or sin is already necessitated. How does this reality affect your dua (supplication)? Do you pray with the same urgency knowing that even your prayer itself is determined? Or does this knowledge drive you to plead more earnestly for the preponderant factor of divine mercy to incline your heart toward obedience?
?
The third division of the argument—that the preponderant factor comes from neither God nor servant—is rejected because it would mean events happen without an originator. But consider: have you ever acted as if your own choices arise from nowhere, as if you are the originator of your own will? In what area of your life are you most likely to forget that every impetus, even your own desire, comes ultimately from God? How can you remind yourself of this dependency today?

The Servant's Inability: From Possibility to Determinism
Razi argues that even granting the servant's ability to refrain, determinism still follows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second argument: even if the servant can possibly refrain, the preponderance factor leads to determinism whether it depends on a factor or not.

Core Idea
Whether the servant's preponderance depends on a factor or occurs by chance, determinism is inevitable.

Razi now considers a different starting point: suppose the servant, while being the source of the act, can possibly refrain. He then examines whether the preponderance to act depends on a preponderant factor or not. In both cases, he argues, determinism follows—either through infinite regress or through chance necessitating the act. This clinches the Ash'ari conclusion that the servant cannot truly choose otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Read the second portion of the passage
Focus on the text beginning with 'هذا كله إذا قلنا بأن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل يصح منه الترك'. Understand that Razi now assumes the servant can possibly refrain.
This is a different assumption from the first portion.
2
Trace the two sub-cases
Razi divides the scenario into two: either the preponderance depends on a preponderant factor or it does not. Follow each branch to its conclusion.
The first branch leads to infinite regress and determinism; the second leads to preponderance by chance, which also necessitates determinism.
3
Understand the conclusion
The final two sentences state that when the servant is the source of the act, refraining is impossible, and when the source of refraining, acting is impossible. That is the deterministic outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : ثبت أن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل. إن صح الترك فإما أن يتوقف ذلك الترجيح على المرجح أو لا يتوقف، وثبت أن القسمين باطلان، فثبت أن العبد حال كونه مصدرا للفعل يمتنع منه الترك. وحال كونه مصدرا للترك، يمتنع منه الفعل.
The twenty-second issue. If the preponderant factor exists, the act becomes necessary of occurrence, and on the assumption that it does not occur, the act becomes impossible of occurrence. If the second is the truth, that it did not reach the limit of necessity. We say: If such is the case, then when that preponderant factor is present, it is not impossible for that act to occur sometimes and not occur at other times. And everything that is possible, it is not necessary from assuming its occurrence an absurdity. So let us assume it sometimes occurring and sometimes not occurring. The specification of one of the two times by occurrence and the second by non-occurrence either depends on the addition of an extra condition or does not depend. If it depends, then what first occurred was not the complete preponderant factor, because this condition was necessarily with it. But we had assumed what first occurred to be the complete preponderant factor—that is a contradiction. Also, the division returns to the aggregate consisting of the first preponderant factor and this condition. If the preponderance does not become necessary, it requires another preponderant factor, leading to infinite regress—which is impossible. And if it becomes necessary, then what we mentioned of the necessity of determinism returns. But if the specification of one of the two times by occurrence does not depend on the addition of an extra condition to what was first present, while the relation of that preponderant factor which was first present to the two times of occurrence and non-occurrence is equal, then the preponderance of one side of the possible over the other without a preponderant factor follows—which is impossible. As for the third division: that the preponderant factor occurs neither from the servant nor from God Almighty; this entails the occurrence of events without an originator, and allowing it invalidates the argument from the occurrence of events for the existence of God Almighty—and this is false. All this if we say that the servant, while being the source of the act, it is possible for him to refrain instead of the act, except that this preponderance depends on a preponderant factor. But if we say that it does not depend on a preponderant factor, then preponderance has occurred without an effective agent, and allowing it invalidates the statement that contingent things need an effective agent and a preponderant factor, and it entails the denial of the Maker. Also, assuming that such is the case, that preponderance must be occurring by chance, meaning it occurs without something issuing from the act. This also entails determinism, because if that chance occurs, the act occurs whether he wills or does not will; if it does not occur, the act does not occur whether he wills or does not will. Thus determinism is necessary on this assumption as well. If you have understood this, we say: It is established that the servant, while being the source of the act, if refraining is possible, then that preponderance either depends on a preponderant factor or does not, and it is established that both divisions are false. Thus it is established that the servant, while being the source of the act, cannot refrain; and while being the source of refraining, cannot act.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument about preponderance (tarjih) and its implications for human free will. Razi begins by considering two possibilities regarding the preponderant factor that determines an act: either the act becomes necessary when the factor is present, or not. He then examines the scenario where the act is possible but requires a preponderant factor. He argues that if the specification of one time over another for occurrence depends on an additional condition, then the initial factor was not truly complete, leading to infinite regress or determinism. If no additional condition is needed but the factor relates equally to both times, then preponderance occurs without cause, which is absurd. A third division—that the preponderant factor comes from neither servant nor God—invalidates the argument for God's existence. Razi then shifts to the condition where the servant can possibly refrain. He shows that if the preponderance depends on a factor, determinism follows via regress; if not, preponderance occurs by chance, again determinism. The conclusion is that when the servant is the source of the act, refraining is impossible; when the source of refraining, acting is impossible. This is a key argument for determinism (jabr) in Ash'ari thought, aiming to show that human acts are ultimately necessitated.

Key Terms
المرجح
الجبر
الاتفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if preponderance occurs by chance, then human free will is preserved.
Correction: Razi shows that chance equally leads to determinism: the act occurs or not independent of the servant's will.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is the consequence if the preponderance does not depend on a preponderant factor?
A) The servant freely chooses the act.
B) The act occurs by chance, and determinism still follows.
C) The act is impossible.
D) The servant's will becomes the effective agent.

Key Takeaway
Even if the servant can possibly refrain, the preponderance to act—whether dependent on a factor or by chance—inevitably leads to determinism, showing that true free will is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading Razi's proof, do you truly believe that your choices are your own? How does this affect your attitude towards your sins? Will you still strive to obey, knowing that your action is ultimately from God? How does this change your reliance on Him rather than your own strength?
?
If the occurrence of an act is necessary regardless of your will, what is the point of dua (supplication)? Does this argument challenge your practice of asking Allah for guidance? How do you reconcile this with the command to use your will?
?
Razi argues that chance leads to determinism. Do you see moments in your life where you attribute things to 'luck' rather than to the decree of Allah? How does this passage call you to a deeper tawakkul (trust)?

Second Proof: Ignorance of One's Own Actions
Razi proves that humans cannot create their actions because they lack detailed knowledge of them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second proof that humans cannot create their own actions because they lack detailed knowledge of those actions.

Core Idea
If we created our actions, we would know every detail—but we don't.

Razi presents a tightly reasoned deductive argument: if a person were truly the creator of their own acts, they would have complete knowledge of those acts, including precise quantities and qualities. Since we clearly lack such detailed awareness of our movements, we cannot be the true originators. This passage unpacks that logical implication and provides vivid examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the core argument is complete.
2
Identify the main premise
Razi states: if the servant were the originator of his actions, he would know their details. Notice how he explains why intention requires knowledge of quantity.
The example of intending ten vs. five vs. twenty clarifies the link.
3
Examine the two examples of ignorance
First example: a sleeping person turns over without knowing the details. Second example: the ant's slow motion involves rests between atomic motions, but the ant has no knowledge.
The second example is incomplete in this passage but the point is clear.
4
Reflect on the Ash'ari concept of kasb
Consider how this proof supports the Ash'ari position that God creates actions while humans acquire them. The proof does not deny human agency, only that humans are the ultimate creators.
This connects to the broader debate on free will and predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لو كان العبد موجدا لأفعال نفسه لكان عالما بتفاصيل أفعاله . وهو غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه، فوجب أن لا يكون موجدا لها . بيان الملازمة: أنه لكونه قادرًا يصح منه وقوع ذلك الفعل بذلك المقدار، ويصح وقوعه أزيد منه أو أنقص منه فوقوع ذلك المقدار دون ما هو أزيد منه أو دون ما هو أنقص منه، لا يكون إلا لأجل القصد والاختيار والقصد والاختيار مشروط بالعلم، لأن القصد إلى إيجاد العشرة فوق الخمسة، ودون العشرين، لا يتأتى إلا مع العلم بأنه عشرة، وليس بخمسة، وليس بعشرين فثبت أن العبد لو كان موجدا لأفعال نفسه لكان عالما بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه وهذا هو معنى قوله سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ﴾ [الملك: ١٤]. وإنما قلنا : إن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه لوجوه : أحدها: أن النائم والمغمى عليه قد ينقلب من أحد جنبيه إلى الجنب الآخر ، مع أنه ليس له من كمية تلك الأفعال ولا كيفيتها خبر البتة. والثاني: أن أكثر المتكلمين متوافقون في إثبات الجوهر الفرد، ومتى ثبت القول بالجوهر الفرد كان التفاوت بين الحركات في البطء والسرعة، لأجل تخلل السكنات فيما بين الحركات وسيأتي البرهان على ذلك في تقرير مسألة الجوهر الفرد وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : النملة إذا تحركت بحركة بطيئة فذاك لأنها تحركت في بعض
The second proof: If the servant were the originator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his actions. But he is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions, so it is necessary that he is not their originator. Explanation of the implication: Because he is capable, it is possible for him to perform that act with that quantity, and it is possible for him to perform it greater or less than that. So the occurrence of that quantity rather than what is greater or less than it is only due to intention and choice. Intention and choice are conditioned by knowledge, because intending to bring about ten above five and below twenty is only possible with knowledge that it is ten, not five, and not twenty. Thus it is established that if the servant were the originator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. And this is the meaning of His saying, Exalted and High: 'Does He who created not know, and He is the Subtle, the Aware?' [Qur'an 67:14]. And we say that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions for reasons: One of them: The sleeper and the unconscious person may turn from one side to the other, while they have absolutely no awareness of the quantity or quality of those actions. The second: That most theologians agree on the affirmation of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard), and once the affirmation of the indivisible atom is established, the variation among motions in slowness and speed is due to the interposition of rests (sakanāt) between the motions. The proof of that will come in the discussion of the indivisible atom. And when this is established, we say: The ant, when it moves with a slow motion, that is because it moves in some...
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a formal proof (al-ḥujja al-thāniya) against the idea that humans create their own acts. Razi's argument: 1) Premise: If the servant were the creator of his actions, he would have detailed knowledge of them. He explains the connection: A capable agent can perform an act with a specific quantity; the selection of that quantity over others requires intention (qaṣd) and choice (ikhtiyār), which in turn require knowledge of the quantity. For example, intending ten requires knowing it is ten and not five or twenty. 2) Second premise: The servant does not have such detailed knowledge. He gives two examples: (a) A sleeping or unconscious person turns over without knowing the details; (b) The existence of indivisible atoms (jawhar fard) implies that speed variation comes from rests between atomic motions, and an ant's slow motion involves many such rests, yet the ant has no knowledge of its detailed motions. The proof is incomplete in this window, but the structure is clear: the servant's ignorance of his actions' details negates his being their originator. He cites the Quranic verse as support. This argument is used to defend the Ash'ari position that God is the true creator of all actions, while humans 'acquire' them (kasb).

Key Terms
موجد
تفاصيل الأفعال
القصد
الاختيار
العلم
الجوهر الفرد
السكنات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof denies human agency entirely.
Correction: Razi only denies that humans create the details; in Ash'ari theology, humans still 'acquire' the act (kasb), meaning they are responsible but not creators.

Checkpoint
What example does Razi give to show that humans lack detailed knowledge of their own actions?
A) A person writing a book.
B) A sleeper turning over in bed.
C) A builder constructing a house.
D) A scholar teaching students.

Key Takeaway
Human lack of detailed knowledge of their own actions proves that they are not the true creators of those actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent action you performed—maybe a conversation, a meal, or a prayer. Did you know every detail of how your muscles moved, how your voice sounded, or how the food was digested? If not, how does this proof strip away any sense of self-sufficiency in your daily life? Will you pause today to acknowledge that every detail is from Allah?
?
When you succeed in something, do you subtly credit your own intelligence or effort? This proof shows you are ignorant of even the basic details of your own actions. How can you use this awareness to genuinely thank Allah for every small accomplishment? Write one specific way you will express this gratitude today.
?
The sleeper turns over without knowing—what does that say about your actions that happen automatically? Are you fully accountable for them? How does this proof change your view of your own responsibility? Commit to asking Allah for forgiveness for any action whose details you were unaware of but still may have been sinful.

Razi's Refutation of the Analogy Between Witnessed and Unseen
Razi answers the objection that God would be a necessitating cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the analogy between human and divine action by distinguishing between originated will and eternal will.

Core Idea
God's eternal will breaks the chain of causal regress.

This passage presents a key objection to Razi's position on divine action and his answer. The objector argues that if human actions are compelled by a chain of wills, then God must also be a necessitating cause. Razi's response hinges on the nature of God's will being eternal, unlike human wills that are originated and require a cause. Understanding this distinction is crucial for defending divine voluntary action.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector claims that the same reasoning applied to human actions in the witnessed realm forces the same conclusion for God in the unseen realm: God must be a necessitating cause.
The objector uses the principle of analogy (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid).
2
Identify Razi's key distinction
Razi points out that human will is originated (muhdatha) while God's will is eternal (qadima). This difference is crucial.
3
Trace the regress argument for human will
If human will is originated, it requires an originator. If that originator is the human themselves, we get an infinite regress, which is impossible. Therefore, wills must end in a necessary will created by Allah, implying compulsion.
This shows that humans are not independent agents.
4
Contrast with divine will
God's will is eternal, so it does not require an originator. Thus, God acts by choice, not necessity.
The analogy fails because the two wills are fundamentally different.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : هذا الذي ذكرتم في الشاهد يلزمكم مثله في الغائب، فوجب أن يكون الباري تعالى علة موجبة بالذات لا فاعلا بالاختيار. قلنا الفرق بين الشاهد والغائب أن صدور الفعل عن القادر موقوف على الإرادة. وهذه إرادة في الشاهد ،محدثة، فافتقرت إلى محدث فإن كان ذلك المحدث هو العبد لزم التسلسل . وهو محال فوجب القول بانتهاء الإرادات إلى إرادة ضرورية، يخلقها الله تعالى في العبد ابتداء. وعند هذا يصير الجبر لازما أما إرادة الله تعالى فهي قديمة عندنا، فاستغنت تلك الإرادة لأجل قدمها عن إرادة أخرى فظهر الفرق بين الصورتين
If it is said: This that you have mentioned in the witnessed (shahid) necessitates the same for you in the unseen (gha'ib), so it must be that the Exalted Creator is a cause necessitating by essence (illa mujiba bi al-dhat), not an agent by choice (fa'il bi al-ikhtiyar). We say: The difference between the witnessed and the unseen is that the occurrence of the act from the capable (qadir) depends on will (irada). And this will, in the witnessed, is originated (muhdatha), so it needs an originator (muhdith). If that originator is the servant, then infinite regress (tasalsul) follows, which is impossible. So it is necessary to say that wills terminate in a necessary will (irada daruriyya) which Allah creates in the servant initially. And at this point, compulsion (jabr) becomes necessary. As for the will of Allah, it is eternal (qadima) with us, so that will, due to its eternity, is independent of another will. Thus the difference between the two cases appears.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (refutation). The objector claims that the earlier argument about human actions applying to the witnessed (shahid) realm forces the same conclusion in the unseen (gha'ib) realm: if a human is compelled in the witnessed, then God must be a necessitating cause (illa mujiba bi al-dhat) in the unseen, rather than an agent by choice (fa'il bi al-ikhtiyar). Razi answers by distinguishing the two realms. He states that the occurrence of an act from a capable agent depends on will (irada). In the witnessed, the will is originated (muhdatha), so it requires an originator (muhdith). If that originator were the servant himself, an infinite regress would result, which is impossible. Therefore, wills must terminate in a necessary will (irada daruriyya) that Allah creates in the servant initially, which entails compulsion (jabr). However, Allah's will is eternal (qadima), so it is independent of any other will. This difference shows why the analogy fails: human actions depend on created wills that require a creator, while divine action depends on an eternal will requiring no further cause.

Key Terms
الشاهد
الغائب
العلة الموجبة بالذات
الفاعل بالاختيار
الإرادة المحدثة
الإرادة القديمة
التسلسل
الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any causal necessity eliminates free agency.
Correction: Razi shows that eternal will does not require a cause, so God's action is voluntary despite being necessary in a sense.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why must God be a necessitating cause like human actions?
A) Because both are agents in the same realm.
B) Because the same reasoning applies to both the witnessed and the unseen.
C) Because God's will is eternal.
D) Because the servant's will is originated.

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the analogy by contrasting originated human will, which requires a cause and leads to compulsion, with eternal divine will, which is self-sufficient and preserves voluntary agency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a choice, do you acknowledge that your very will to choose is created by Allah, or do you take pride in your own independence? How would recognizing this affect your humility before Him?
?
If Allah’s will is eternal and independent, does that make you trust His decisions more, even when you don’t understand them? Where in your life do you struggle to submit to His decree?
?
You believe that your evil deeds are not compelled by Allah, yet your will is created by Him. Does this thought drive you to seek His help in every good action, or do you rely on your own strength? What change in your daily routine would reflect true reliance on Allah?

The Logical Core and the Sleeper's Example
Razi presents the logical argument and the first of four reasons showing lack of detailed knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical entailment that if humans created their actions they would need detailed knowledge, and how the sleeper's movement demonstrates our ignorance.

Core Idea
If we created our actions, we would know every detail—but we don't, so we don't.

Imam Razi begins the second proof by establishing a necessary link between creation and knowledge. He explains that a capable agent's specific act requires intention and choice, which depend on knowledge. He then provides the first of several examples: a sleeping person who moves without any awareness of the movement's details. This lesson covers the main argument and the simplest evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the logical flow: if A then B, not B, so not A.
The passage includes a Quranic citation at the end.
2
Understand the entailment
The key is the phrase 'بيان الملازمة'. Razi argues that a specific measure of an act (e.g., ten) requires intention, which requires knowledge of the measure. Without that knowledge, intention is impossible.
Think about the example of intending to create ten: you must know it is ten, not five or twenty.
3
Analyze the sleeper example
The first reason: a sleeper or unconscious person turns over without any knowledge of the quantity or quality of the movement. This shows we can perform complex actions without detailed awareness.
This example is simple but powerful—it shows that actions can occur without the actor's detailed knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : لو كان العبد موجدا لأفعال نفسه لكان عالما بتفاصيل أفعاله . وهو غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه، فوجب أن لا يكون موجدا لها . بيان الملازمة: أنه لكونه قادرًا يصح منه وقوع ذلك الفعل بذلك المقدار، ويصح وقوعه أزيد منه أو أنقص منه فوقوع ذلك المقدار دون ما هو أزيد منه أو دون ما هو أنقص منه، لا يكون إلا لأجل القصد والاختيار والقصد والاختيار مشروط بالعلم، لأن القصد إلى إيجاد العشرة فوق الخمسة، ودون العشرين، لا يتأتى إلا مع العلم بأنه عشرة، وليس بخمسة، وليس بعشرين فثبت أن العبد لو كان موجدا لأفعال نفسه لكان عالما بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه وهذا هو معنى قوله سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ﴾ [الملك: ١٤]. وإنما قلنا : إن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه لوجوه : أحدها: أن النائم والمغمى عليه قد ينقلب من أحد جنبيه إلى الجنب الآخر ، مع أنه ليس له من كمية تلك الأفعال ولا كيفيتها خبر البتة. والثاني: أن أكثر المتكلمين متوافقون في إثبات الجوهر الفرد، ومتى ثبت القول بالجوهر الفرد كان التفاوت بين الحركات في البطء والسرعة، لأجل تخلل السكنات فيما بين الحركات وسيأتي البرهان على ذلك في تقرير مسألة الجوهر الفرد وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : النملة إذا تحركت بحركة بطيئة فذاك لأنها تحركت في بعض الأحياز وسكنت في بعضها ومعلوم أنه ليس عند النملة خبر من كمية عدد تلك الأحياز، وليس عندها خبر من أنها سكنت ههنا وتحركت هناك، والحال في الآدمي الذي هو أعقل الحيوانات كذلك فإنه إذا مشى فلا شك أن مشيه أبطأ من حركة الفلك. وذلك لأنه سكن في بعض الأحياز، وتحرك في بعضها. وهذا الذي هو أعقل الخلق، لو أراد أن يعرف أنه أين سكن؟ وأين تحرك؟ لم يعرف فعلمنا أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أحوال فعله. الثالث : أن مذهب أبي علي و أبي هاشم : أن الجسم، إذا تحرك، فهناك ثلاثة أمور : الجسم والمتحركية والحركة. وهذه الحركة معنى توجب المتحركية. وتأثير قدرة العبد ليس في نفس المتحركية، بل في هذا المعنى الذي يوجب المتحركية. ومعلوم أن أكثر العقلاء غافلون عن هذا الثالث ولا يخطر ببالهم، ولا يدور في خيالهم تصور هذا الثالث وإذا ثبت كونهم غافلين عن ماهيته، استحال القصد إلى إيجاده وتكوينه. فإن ما لا يكون متصورًا عند الذهن امتنع القصد إلى إيجاده. وهذا الوجه الثاني والثالث مختص بمشايخ المعتزلة. فأما أبو الحسين فإنه متوقف في الجوهر الفرد وناف لهذا المعنى الثالث. فلا يلزمه ذلك. الرابع: أن من حرك إصبعه فلا شك أن ذلك الإصبع مركب من الأجزاء. وقامت بكل واحدة منها حركة على حدة فإذا لزم فيمن يوجد الشيء أن يكون عالما بتفاصيله من الكمية والكيفية وجب في محرك هذا الإصبع أن يكون عالما بأن أجزاء هذا الإصبع كم هي ؟ حتى يمكنه القصد إلى إيجاد الحركة في كل واحد من الأجزاء، ويكون عالمًا بعدد الأحياز الواقعة من مبدأ الحركة إلى منتهاها، حتى يمكنه القصد إلى إيجاد الحركات في تلك الأحياز، ولما لم يكن شيء من هذه الأحوال معلوما علمنا أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : ظهر أنه لو كان موجدا لأفعال نفسه، لكان عالما بتفاصيل تلك الأفعال، وظهر أنه غير عالم بتفاصيلها، فوجب القطع بأن العبد غير موجد لها
The second proof: If the servant were the creator (mujid) of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his actions. But he is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions, so it is necessary that he is not their creator. Explanation of the entailment: Because he is capable (qadir), it is valid from him the occurrence of that act with that measure, and it is valid its occurrence greater or lesser. So the occurrence of that measure without what is greater or lesser is only due to intention (qasd) and choice (ikhtiyar). And intention and choice are conditioned by knowledge, because intending to create ten more than five and less than twenty only occurs with knowledge that it is ten, not five, and not twenty. So it is established that if the servant were the creator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. And this is the meaning of His saying, Exalted and High: 'Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware' [Quran 67:14]. And we only said that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions for several reasons: First: The sleeper and the unconscious may turn from one side to the other, while they have no information at all about the quantity or quality of those actions. Second: Most theologians (mutakallimun) agree on affirming the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). And when the view of the indivisible atom is established, the difference between movements in slowness and speed is due to the interposition of rests (sakanat) between the movements, and the proof for that will come in the discussion of the indivisible atom. And when this is established, we say: The ant, when it moves with a slow movement, that is because it moved in some spaces (ahya') and rested in some, and it is known that the ant has no information about the quantity of the number of those spaces, nor does it have information about that it rested here and moved there. And the case of the human, who is the most intelligent of animals, is similar. When he walks, there is no doubt that his walking is slower than the movement of the sphere. That is because he rested in some spaces and moved in some. This one, who is the most intelligent of creation, if he wanted to know where he rested and where he moved, he would not know. So we know that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of the states of his action. Third: The doctrine of Abu Ali and Abu Hashim is that, when the body moves, there are three things: the body, the state of being moved (mutaharrikiyya), and the movement (haraka). And this movement is a meaning (ma'na) that necessitates the state of being moved. And the effect of the servant's power is not on the state of being moved itself, but rather on this meaning that necessitates the state of being moved. And it is known that most rational people are heedless of this third thing, and it does not occur to their minds, nor does the conception of this third thing circulate in their imaginations. And if it is established that they are heedless of its essence, then intending to bring it into existence and create it is impossible. That which is not conceived in the mind, intending its bringing into existence is prevented. And this second and third reason are specific to the masters of the Mu'tazila. As for Abu al-Husayn, he is suspensive about the indivisible atom and denies this third meaning, so that does not apply to him. Fourth: He who moves his finger, there is no doubt that that finger is composed of parts, and in each one of them a movement occurs separately. So if it is necessary that the one who brings something into existence be knowledgeable of its details in quantity and quality, then it would be necessary for the mover of this finger to know how many parts of this finger are, so that he can intend to create movement in each one of the parts, and be knowledgeable of the number of spaces occurring from the beginning of the movement to its end, so that he can intend to create movements in those spaces. And since none of these states are known, we know that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. And when this is established, we say: It has become clear that if he were the creator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of those actions, and it has become clear that he is not knowledgeable of their details, so it is necessary to be certain that the servant is not their creator.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof (al-hujja al-thaniya) that the servant does not create his own actions. The argument is: if the servant were the creator (mujid) of his actions, he would have to know their details (tafasil). But he does not know their details, so he cannot be their creator. Razi first explains the entailment: a capable agent (qadir) can perform an act with a specific measure, or greater or lesser. The specific occurrence is due to intention (qasd) and choice (ikhtiyar), and these require knowledge of the act's details. For example, intending to create ten requires knowing it is ten, not five or twenty. Then he confirms the minor premise—that the servant lacks detailed knowledge—by giving four reasons (wujuh). The first reason: the sleeper or unconscious person turns over without any awareness of the quantity or quality of the movement. The second reason: theologians affirm the indivisible atom (jawhar fard); difference in speed is due to rests between movements. The ant's slow movement involves moving in some spaces and resting in others, but the ant has no knowledge of the number of spaces. Similarly, a human walking slower than the celestial sphere has no knowledge of where he rested. The third reason: according to Abu Ali and Abu Hashim, when a body moves, there are three things: the body, the property of being moved (mutaharrikiyya), and the movement itself (haraka). The servant's power only affects the movement meaning (ma'na), not the property. Most people are unaware of this third thing, so they cannot intend to create it. This reason is specific to Mu'tazili scholars; Abu al-Husayn rejects the atom and thus this point. The fourth reason: moving a finger composed of parts requires knowing the number of parts and spaces to intend each movement, but we lack such knowledge. Therefore, since man lacks knowledge of his action details, he cannot be their creator. The conclusion is certain: the servant does not create his actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person knows exactly what he is doing when he performs an action.
Correction: Razi shows that even simple actions like turning over in sleep occur without any detailed awareness, so we cannot claim full knowledge of our actions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the necessary condition for intention (qasd) and choice (ikhtiyar)?
A) Power
B) Knowledge
C) Action
D) Movement

Key Takeaway
If we created our own actions, we would need detailed knowledge of them; since we lack that knowledge (as shown by the sleeper), we are not the creators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a recent action you performed without fully knowing its details—like a habit or a reaction. How does that reveal your lack of complete control? What does that teach you about your dependence on Allah's creation of your actions?
?
You often assume you are the author of your choices. But if you cannot describe every detail of even a simple movement, what does that say about your claim to self-sufficiency? Are you willing to admit that your very ability to choose is a gift from the All-Knowing?
?
Razi's sleeper turns over without knowledge. In what areas of your daily life do you act like a sleeper, unaware of the full reality of your deeds? How can this lesson lead you to thank Allah for His knowledge and power?

Atomism, Movement, and the Finger Example
Razi presents three further reasons based on atomism, Mu'tazilite metaphysics, and anatomy, then concludes the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three further reasons from atomistic physics and anatomy that show humans lack detailed knowledge of their actions, confirming that God alone creates.

Core Idea
We are ignorant of atomic rests, the nature of movement, and the parts of our own finger—so we cannot create these actions.

Razi continues with more sophisticated arguments. He draws on the concept of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) to show that differences in speed involve rests between movements, which we do not perceive. He then presents the Mu'tazilite analysis of movement into three components, and finally the example of moving a finger whose parts we do not know. These reasons reinforce the conclusion that we cannot be the creators of our actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note that it contains three distinct reasons (second, third, fourth).
The passage also mentions the Mu'tazilite background and an exception for Abu al-Husayn.
2
Understand the atomism argument
The second reason: speed differences are due to rests between atomic movements. The ant's slow movement involves many spaces and rests, but the ant has no knowledge of them. Similarly, humans walking slower than the sphere do not know where they rested.
This argument depends on the existence of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard).
3
Analyze the three aspects of motion
The third reason: according to Abu Ali and Abu Hashim, when a body moves there are three things: body, being-moved, and movement. The servant's power affects only the movement meaning. Most people are unaware of this third entity, so they cannot intend to create it.
This reason is specific to Mu'tazili theologians; Abu al-Husayn rejects it.
4
Examine the finger example
The fourth reason: moving a finger composed of parts requires knowing the number of parts and spaces to intend each movement. Since we lack that knowledge, we cannot be the creators.
This is a vivid example that applies to everyday actions.
5
Draw the conclusion
After presenting four reasons, Razi restates the main argument: we lack detailed knowledge, so we are not creators.
The conclusion is certain: 'فوجب القطع بأن العبد غير موجد لها'.

الحجة الثانية : لو كان العبد موجدا لأفعال نفسه لكان عالما بتفاصيل أفعاله . وهو غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه، فوجب أن لا يكون موجدا لها . بيان الملازمة: أنه لكونه قادرًا يصح منه وقوع ذلك الفعل بذلك المقدار، ويصح وقوعه أزيد منه أو أنقص منه فوقوع ذلك المقدار دون ما هو أزيد منه أو دون ما هو أنقص منه، لا يكون إلا لأجل القصد والاختيار والقصد والاختيار مشروط بالعلم، لأن القصد إلى إيجاد العشرة فوق الخمسة، ودون العشرين، لا يتأتى إلا مع العلم بأنه عشرة، وليس بخمسة، وليس بعشرين فثبت أن العبد لو كان موجدا لأفعال نفسه لكان عالما بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه وهذا هو معنى قوله سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ﴾ [الملك: ١٤]. وإنما قلنا : إن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه لوجوه : أحدها: أن النائم والمغمى عليه قد ينقلب من أحد جنبيه إلى الجنب الآخر ، مع أنه ليس له من كمية تلك الأفعال ولا كيفيتها خبر البتة. والثاني: أن أكثر المتكلمين متوافقون في إثبات الجوهر الفرد، ومتى ثبت القول بالجوهر الفرد كان التفاوت بين الحركات في البطء والسرعة، لأجل تخلل السكنات فيما بين الحركات وسيأتي البرهان على ذلك في تقرير مسألة الجوهر الفرد وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : النملة إذا تحركت بحركة بطيئة فذاك لأنها تحركت في بعض الأحياز وسكنت في بعضها ومعلوم أنه ليس عند النملة خبر من كمية عدد تلك الأحياز، وليس عندها خبر من أنها سكنت ههنا وتحركت هناك، والحال في الآدمي الذي هو أعقل الحيوانات كذلك فإنه إذا مشى فلا شك أن مشيه أبطأ من حركة الفلك. وذلك لأنه سكن في بعض الأحياز، وتحرك في بعضها. وهذا الذي هو أعقل الخلق، لو أراد أن يعرف أنه أين سكن؟ وأين تحرك؟ لم يعرف فعلمنا أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أحوال فعله. الثالث : أن مذهب أبي علي و أبي هاشم : أن الجسم، إذا تحرك، فهناك ثلاثة أمور : الجسم والمتحركية والحركة. وهذه الحركة معنى توجب المتحركية. وتأثير قدرة العبد ليس في نفس المتحركية، بل في هذا المعنى الذي يوجب المتحركية. ومعلوم أن أكثر العقلاء غافلون عن هذا الثالث ولا يخطر ببالهم، ولا يدور في خيالهم تصور هذا الثالث وإذا ثبت كونهم غافلين عن ماهيته، استحال القصد إلى إيجاده وتكوينه. فإن ما لا يكون متصورًا عند الذهن امتنع القصد إلى إيجاده. وهذا الوجه الثاني والثالث مختص بمشايخ المعتزلة. فأما أبو الحسين فإنه متوقف في الجوهر الفرد وناف لهذا المعنى الثالث. فلا يلزمه ذلك. الرابع: أن من حرك إصبعه فلا شك أن ذلك الإصبع مركب من الأجزاء. وقامت بكل واحدة منها حركة على حدة فإذا لزم فيمن يوجد الشيء أن يكون عالما بتفاصيله من الكمية والكيفية وجب في محرك هذا الإصبع أن يكون عالما بأن أجزاء هذا الإصبع كم هي ؟ حتى يمكنه القصد إلى إيجاد الحركة في كل واحد من الأجزاء، ويكون عالمًا بعدد الأحياز الواقعة من مبدأ الحركة إلى منتهاها، حتى يمكنه القصد إلى إيجاد الحركات في تلك الأحياز، ولما لم يكن شيء من هذه الأحوال معلوما علمنا أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : ظهر أنه لو The second proof: If the servant were the creator (mujid) of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his actions. But he is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions, so it is necessary that he is not their creator. Explanation of the entailment: Because he is capable (qadir), it is valid from him the occurrence of that act with that measure, and it is valid its occurrence greater or lesser. So the occurrence of that measure without what is greater or lesser is only due to intention (qasd) and choice (ikhtiyar). And intention and choice are conditioned by knowledge, because intending to create ten more than five and less than twenty only occurs with knowledge that it is ten, not five, and not twenty. So it is established that if the servant were the creator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. And this is the meaning of His saying, Exalted and High: 'Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware' [Quran 67:14]. And we only said that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions for several reasons: First: The sleeper and the unconscious may turn from one side to the other, while they have no information at all about the quantity or quality of those actions. Second: Most theologians (mutakallimun) agree on affirming the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). And when the view of the indivisible atom is established, the difference between movements in slowness and speed is due to the interposition of rests (sakanat) between the movements, and the proof for that will come in the discussion of the indivisible atom. And when this is established, we say: The ant, when it moves with a slow movement, that is because it moved in some spaces (ahya') and rested in some, and it is known that the ant has no information about the quantity of the number of those spaces, nor does it have information about that it rested here and moved there. And the case of the human, who is the most intelligent of animals, is similar. When he walks, there is no doubt that his walking is slower than the movement of the sphere. That is because he rested in some spaces and moved in some. This one, who is the most intelligent of creation, if he wanted to know where he rested and where he moved, he would not know. So we know that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of the states of his action. Third: The doctrine of Abu Ali and Abu Hashim is that, when the body moves, there are three things: the body, the state of being moved (mutaharrikiyya), and the movement (haraka). And this movement is a meaning (ma'na) that necessitates the state of being moved. And the effect of the servant's power is not on the state of being moved itself, but rather on this meaning that necessitates the state of being moved. And it is known that most rational people are heedless of this third thing, and it does not occur to their minds, nor does the conception of this third thing circulate in their imaginations. And if it is established that they are heedless of its essence, then intending to bring it into existence and create it is impossible. That which is not conceived in the mind, intending its bringing into existence is prevented. And this second and third reason are specific to the masters of the Mu'tazila. As for Abu al-Husayn, he is suspensive about the indivisible atom and denies this third meaning, so that does not apply to him. Fourth: He who moves his finger, there is no doubt that that finger is composed of parts, and in each one of them a movement occurs separately. So if it is necessary that the one who brings something into existence be knowledgeable of its details in quantity and quality, then it would be necessary for the mover of this finger to know how many parts of this finger are, so that he can intend to create movement in each one of the parts, and be knowledgeable of the number of spaces occurring from the beginning of the movement to its end, so that he can intend to create movements in those spaces. And since none of these states are known, we know that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. And when this is established, we say: It has become clear that if he were the creator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of those actions, and it has become clear that he is not knowledgeable of their details, so it is necessary to be certain that the servant is not their creator.

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof (al-hujja al-thaniya) that the servant does not create his own actions. The argument is: if the servant were the creator (mujid) of his actions, he would have to know their details (tafasil). But he does not know their details, so he cannot be their creator. For example, intending to create ten requires knowing it is ten, not five or twenty. Then he confirms the minor premise—that the servant lacks detailed knowledge—by giving four reasons (wujuh). The first reason: the sleeper or unconscious person turns over without any awareness of the quantity or quality of the movement. The second reason: theologians affirm the indivisible atom (jawhar fard); difference in speed is due to rests between movements. The ant's slow movement involves moving in some spaces and resting in others, but the ant has no knowledge of the number of spaces. Similarly, a human walking slower than the celestial sphere has no knowledge of where he rested. The third reason: according to Abu Ali and Abu Hashim, when a body moves, there are three things: the body, the property of being moved (mutaharrikiyya), and the movement itself (haraka). The servant's power only affects the movement meaning (ma'na), not the property. Most people are unaware of this third thing, so they cannot intend to create it. This reason is specific to Mu'tazili scholars; Abu al-Husayn rejects the atom and thus this point. The fourth reason: moving a finger composed of parts requires knowing the number of parts and spaces to intend each movement, but we lack such knowledge. Therefore, since man lacks knowledge of his action details, he cannot be their creator. The conclusion is certain: the servant does not create his actions.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: We have complete control and knowledge over our movements like walking or moving a finger.

What does the example of the ant moving slowly demonstrate?
A) Ants are intelligent creatures.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You move your finger right now. Do you truly know how many parts it has or what happens at the atomic level? If you don't, can you honestly claim to be the creator of that movement? Then who is? How does this reshape your understanding of your daily actions?
?
Razi says even the most intelligent person is ignorant of the atomic rests in a simple walk. When you walk to the mosque, do you ever think about the divine power sustaining each step? ?

Divine Decree

The Proof from Ignorance of Action Details
Razi presents a four-part proof from ignorance of action details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that humans cannot be the creators of their actions because they lack knowledge of the detailed physical components and states of those actions.

Core Idea
Ignorance of action details proves we are not their creators.

In this passage from Al-Arba'een, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi combines multiple examples and logical reasoning to argue against the idea that humans create their own actions. He uses the movement of an ant, the walking of a human, and the subtle ontology of certain Mu'tazilites to show that if we were truly creators, we would need complete knowledge of every detail—yet we are ignorant. This lesson walks through each part of his proof and its conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify its parts
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Razi presents a 'twenty-second issue' and then gives the second, third, and fourth aspects of a proof. The first aspect is not included here.
The second aspect uses the ant example, the third involves Mu'tazilite ontology, and the fourth involves moving a finger.
2
Understand the logical structure
The overall argument is a conditional proof: if the servant were the creator of his actions, he would be knowledgeable of their details. Since he is not knowledgeable, he is not the creator. Each aspect supports the minor premise (lack of knowledge).
Look for the phrase 'if...then' and 'since it is not the case...then not' in the translation.
3
Analyze the third aspect carefully
The third aspect relies on a specific Mu'tazilite analysis (Abu Ali and Abu Hashim) that distinguishes body, mobility, and motion. Razi argues that most people are unaware of this third element, so they cannot intend to create it.
Razi notes that Abu al-Husayn al-Basri rejects this analysis, so the argument does not apply to him.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
After presenting the examples, Razi states the conclusion clearly: the servant must be judged not to be the creator of his actions. This is a key point in the debate over human free will and divine omnipotence.
This argument is part of the Ash'ari position against the Mu'tazila on the question of human capacity (istita'a).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية والعشرون
من حركة الأحياز وسكنت في بعضها ومعلوم أنه ليس عند النملة خبر من كمية عدد تلك الأحياز، وليس عندها خبر من أنها سكنت ههنا وتحركت هناك، والحال في الآدمي الذي هو أعقل الحيوانات كذلك فإنه إذا مشى فلا شك أن مشيه أبطأ الفلك. وذلك لأنه سكن في بعض الأحياز، وتحرك في بعضها. وهذا الذي هو أعقل الخلق، لو أراد أن يعرف أنه أين سكن؟ وأين تحرك؟ لم يعرف فعلمنا أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أحوال فعله. الثالث : أن مذهب أبي علي و أبي هاشم : أن الجسم، إذا تحرك، فهناك ثلاثة أمور : الجسم والمتحركية والحركة. وهذه الحركة معنى توجب المتحركية. وتأثير قدرة العبد ليس في نفس المتحركية، بل في هذا المعنى الذي يوجب المتحركية. ومعلوم أن أكثر العقلاء غافلون عن هذا الثالث ولا يخطر ببالهم، ولا يدور في خيالهم تصور هذا الثالث وإذا ثبت كونهم غافلين عن ماهيته، استحال القصد إلى إيجاده وتكوينه. فإن ما لا يكون متصورًا عند الذهن امتنع القصد إلى إيجاده. وهذا الوجه الثاني والثالث مختص بمشايخ المعتزلة. فأما أبو الحسين فإنه متوقف في الجوهر الفرد وناف لهذا المعنى الثالث. فلا يلزمه ذلك.
الرابع: أن من حرك إصبعه فلا شك أن ذلك الإصبع مركب من الأجزاء. وقامت بكل واحدة منها حركة على حدة فإذا لزم فيمن يوجد الشيء أن يكون عالما بتفاصيله من الكمية والكيفية وجب في محرك هذا الإصبع أن يكون عالما بأن أجزاء هذا الإصبع كم هي ؟ حتى يمكنه القصد إلى إيجاد الحركة في كل واحد من الأجزاء، ويكون عالمًا بعدد الأحياز الواقعة من مبدأ الحركة إلى منتهاها، حتى يمكنه القصد إلى إيجاد الحركات في تلك الأحياز، ولما لم يكن شيء من هذه الأحوال معلوما علمنا أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه.
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : ظهر أنه لو كان موجدا لأفعال نفسه، لكان عالما بتفاصيل تلك الأفعال، وظهر أنه غير عالم بتفاصيلها، فوجب القطع بأن العبد غير موجد لها
The twenty-second issue. From movement in positions and stillness in some of them, and it is known that the ant has no knowledge of the quantity of the number of those positions, and it has no knowledge that it settled here and moved there. And the situation with the human, who is the most intelligent of animals, is similar: when he walks, there is no doubt that his walking is slower than the sphere. That is because he settles in some positions and moves in some. This one, who is the most intelligent of creation, if he wanted to know where he settled and where he moved, he would not know. So we know that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of the states of his action. Third: that the doctrine of Abu Ali and Abu Hashim is that when the body moves, there are three things: the body, mobility, and motion. And this motion is a meaning that necessitates mobility. And the effect of the servant's power is not in mobility itself, but in this meaning which necessitates mobility. And it is known that most rational beings are heedless of this third [thing] and it does not occur to their minds, nor does the conception of this third revolve in their imagination. And if it is established that they are heedless of its essence, then intending its bringing into existence and creation becomes impossible. For what is not conceived in the mind, intending its bringing into existence is impossible. And these second and third aspects are specific to the shaykhs of the Mu'tazila. As for Abu al-Husayn, he is withholding [judgment] on the indivisible atom and negates this third meaning, so it does not apply to him. Fourth: that if one moves his finger, there is no doubt that that finger is composed of parts. And in each one of them a separate motion occurs. So if it is necessary for the one who brings a thing into existence to be knowledgeable of its details in terms of quantity and quality, then it would be necessary for the mover of this finger to know how many parts this finger has, so that he can intend to bring about motion in each one of the parts, and to know the number of positions occurring from the beginning of the motion to its end, so that he can intend to bring about motions in those positions. And since none of these states are known, we know that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. And if this is established, we say: it appears that if he were the creator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of those actions; and it appears that he is not knowledgeable of their details; so it is necessary to conclusively judge that the servant is not their creator.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents a composite proof that humans cannot be the creators of their own actions, based on their ignorance of the details of those actions. It begins by stating the twenty-second issue (likely the ongoing discussion on human acts). The proof is divided into several aspects (the second, third, and fourth are given here; the first is absent from this window). The second aspect uses the example of an ant moving through positions (positions or loci) without knowing the number of positions or where it settled and moved; similarly, a human walking cannot know every detail of his own movement. The third aspect, specific to the Mu'tazilite masters Abu Ali and Abu Hashim, argues that when a body moves, there are three things: the body, 'mobility' (the state of being moved), and 'motion' (the accident that causes mobility). The servant's power affects only this third thing (motion), but most people are unaware of this third element; thus they cannot intend to create it, as intention requires conception. The author notes that Abu al-Husayn (al-Basri) does not accept the indivisible atom and negates this third meaning, so this argument does not apply to him. The fourth aspect uses the example of moving a finger: the finger is composed of parts, each with its own motion; if one were the creator, he would need to know the exact number of parts and positions to intend each motion. Since people are ignorant of such details, they cannot be creators. The conclusion is that if a servant were the creator of his own actions, he would know their details; but he does not, so he is not the creator. Razi follows the logical structure of conditional proof: if P then Q, but not Q, therefore not P.

Key Terms

النملة
المتحركية
الحركة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People assume they have complete knowledge of their actions and therefore think they are the creators.
Correction: The argument shows that detailed knowledge of the physical process (positions, parts, subtle entities) is beyond human awareness, so we cannot be creators.

?
You have probably never pondered the three entities (body, mobility, motion) during your daily actions. If you cannot conceive what you are supposedly creating, can you truly claim to be its creator? What does this say about your need for the One who is fully aware of every detail?
?
Razi proves that even the most intelligent human is ignorant of the details of his own walking. How does this confront your pride and sense of self-sufficiency? Will you humbly admit that your actions are ultimately from God, and let that transform your reliance on Him?
